3:28:1297:0:70:281:329:708:119:g_d0_f11:119:g_d0_f11:F:Abstract
3:29:1305:70:15:89:540:638:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:During economic downturns, college students can alter their postsecondary education
3:30:1388:15:14:72:540:623:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:decisions through several channels. This paper focuses on college major choice, one higher
3:31:1478:14:15:72:540:609:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:education decision that might change after a recession, and one that few researchers have
3:32:1567:15:14:72:540:594:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:explored. Due to data limitations, previous research is unable to provide definitive results
3:33:1659:14:15:72:540:580:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:on if, or how, matriculating freshmen change college majors during recessions. The data
3:34:1746:15:14:72:540:565:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:used for this study assuages those limitations and is obtained from the “Freshman Survey,”
3:35:1836:14:15:72:540:551:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:administered by the Cooperative Institutional Research Program (CIRP). Building on what
3:36:1923:15:14:72:540:536:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:is already known about how students choose college majors and how they respond to in-
3:37:2008:14:14:72:540:522:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:formation shocks, the theoretical model proposes that during economic downturns, students
3:38:2097:14:15:72:540:508:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:will switch to fields with higher relative wage and employment opportunities. First, this
3:39:2186:15:14:72:540:493:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:study finds that freshmen are less likely to have undeclared intended majors after recessions.
3:40:2280:14:15:72:540:479:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Then, a multinomial logit empirical technique strongly suggests that after economic down-
3:41:2369:15:14:72:539:464:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:turns, those who declare intended majors are more likely to choose ones that offer higher
3:42:2458:14:15:72:540:450:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:wages and provide more job security, like Technology, Business, Engineering and Health.
3:43:2545:15:14:72:540:435:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:University administrators can apply this empirical model to their own institutional-level
3:44:2634:14:15:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:data. In the presence of substantial budget cuts, administrators can anticipate the majors
3:45:2724:15:14:72:540:406:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:that will require more resources and those from which they can transfer resources to effi-
3:46:2814:14:14:72:540:392:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:ciently meet student demand. More broadly, these conclusions offer better information on
3:47:2902:14:15:72:540:378:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:labor force composition after recessions, which can enhance forecasting of likely shortages
3:48:2993:15:0:72:248:363:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and surpluses in the labor market.
4:49:3027:0:36:72:208:708:296:g_d0_f13:296:g_d0_f13:C:1  Introduction
4:50:3042:36:24:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Connections between higher education decisions and the business cycle have garnered the
4:51:3129:24:24:72:540:648:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:attention of researchers, policy makers, and university administrators for decades. Declining
4:52:3222:24:24:72:540:624:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:economic conditions induce university budget cuts, increase student enrollment rates, and
4:53:3311:24:24:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:encourage higher levels of student debt, stretching the resources of postsecondary institutions
4:54:3406:24:24:72:540:576:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and their students (Clark, 2010; Weller, 2012). In the face of tighter budget constraints,
4:55:3496:24:24:72:540:552:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:college students may alter their postsecondary decisions in several ways. This paper focuses
4:56:3588:24:24:72:540:528:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:on college major choice, one particular decision channel that students may adjust during
4:57:3676:24:23:72:540:504:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:recessions, and one which few researches have explored.  Identifying changes in student
4:58:3763:23:24:72:540:481:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:major preferences during economic downturns helps university administrators to anticipate
4:59:3852:24:24:72:540:457:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:demand for certain courses and reduces uncertainity about future labor market shortages
4:60:3939:24:24:72:144:433:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and surpluses.
4:61:3953:24:24:89:540:409:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The “Great Recession” serves as a reminder of how economic downturns constrain higher
4:62:4038:24:24:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:education resources and alter student incentives. Despite the growing education debt, there
4:63:4129:24:24:72:539:361:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:is a renewed effort to increase post-secondary enrollment and graduation rates. In President
4:64:4221:24:24:72:540:337:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Obama’s 2011 Back-To-School Speech, he challenges high school students to continue their
4:65:4309:24:24:72:540:313:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:education after graduation: “...our country used to have the world’s highest proportion of
4:66:4399:24:24:72:540:289:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:young people with a college degree; we now rank 16th. I don’t like being 16th. I like being
4:67:4490:24:24:72:540:265:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:number one.” In addition, the President fostered opportunities for unemployed workers to
4:68:4578:24:23:72:540:241:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:return to school through programs that give special Federal PELL Grant consideration to
4:69:4665:23:24:72:357:218:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:those collecting unemployment insurance (Budd, 2009).
4:70:4718:24:24:89:563:194:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f14:A:Private organizations−like the Lumina Foundation for Education and the Gates Foundation−
4:71:4806:24:24:71:539:170:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:also support increasing the number of college degree attaining citizens. The Lumina Big Goal
4:72:4898:24:24:71:539:146:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:2025 seeks “to increase the percentage of Americans with high-quality degrees and creden-
4:73:4987:24:24:71:539:122:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:tials to 60 percent by the year 2025” (Lumina Foundation, 2012). In the summer of 2012,
4:74:5074:24:0:71:539:98:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the Gates Foundation announced an additional 9 million dollars in grants supporting access
5:75:5165:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:to and completion of higher education degrees (Young, 2012). Initiatives such as these can
5:76:5255:24:24:72:255:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:modify student education decisions.
5:77:5290:24:24:89:539:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:In the wake of the most recent recession, students’ major decisions are under the mi-
5:78:5375:24:24:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:croscope, as many fear that mounting education debt and the inability of students to pay
5:79:5463:24:24:72:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:back college loans will be the next big economic bubble (Cronin and Horton, 2009; Bon-
5:80:5549:24:24:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:ner, 2012).  Contributing to the increasing education loan default rate are the high U.S.
5:81:5638:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:unemployment and underemployment rates for young college graduates, which are now at
5:82:5722:24:24:72:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:all time highs of above 50 percent (Yen, 2012). In July 2012, the National College Finance
5:83:5812:24:24:72:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Center launched the “Don’t Major in Debt” campaign that provides free loan counseling
5:84:5897:24:24:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:for students. Although not an explicit goal of the campaign, the name implies that stu-
5:85:5984:24:23:72:540:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:dents can choose certain college majors that have better long term benefits than others.
5:86:6072:23:24:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Additionally, Carnevale et al. (2012) caution that unemployment risk depends highly on
5:87:6158:24:24:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:undergraduate field of study. Their study reports that after the most recent recession, the
5:88:6249:24:24:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:highest unemployment rates for college graduates are in the Architecture, Arts, and Hu-
5:89:6336:24:24:72:540:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:manities fields; meanwhile, students majoring in fields like Health and Education, enjoy the
5:90:6428:24:24:72:214:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:lowest unemployment rates.
5:91:6454:24:24:89:540:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Due to data limitations, previous research is unable to provide definitive results on if, or
5:92:6546:24:24:72:540:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:how, matriculating freshmen change college majors during recessions. The data used for this
5:93:6637:24:24:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:study assuages those limitations and is obtained from the “Freshman Survey,” administered
5:94:6726:24:24:72:540:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:by the Cooperative Institutional Research Program (CIRP) and housed at the University
5:95:6811:24:24:72:540:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:of California Los Angeles’s (UCLA’s) Higher Education Research Institute (HERI). Only
5:96:6896:24:23:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students’ major intentions are collected, because the survey is limited to college freshman.
5:97:6988:23:24:72:540:182:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Intended majors map to student demand for certain classes and also set students on a major
5:98:7078:24:24:72:540:158:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:track. Once a major is selected, students will incur switching costs if they deviate from that
5:99:7172:24:24:72:135:134:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:initial track.
5:100:7186:24:57:89:539:110:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:This paper tests the hypothesis that after downturns in the business cycle,ceteris paribus,
5:101:7277:57:0:303:309:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:3
6:102:7278:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students will choose majors with better relative income or employment opportunities after
6:103:7367:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:graduation.  For example, after the most recent recession, majors in Health, Education,
6:104:7454:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Business, and Technology were most likely to find jobs, while majors in the Social Sciences,
6:105:7546:24:24:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Arts, and Humanities were least likely to be employed (Associated Press, 2012: Atlantic,
6:106:7634:24:24:72:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:2012). These outcomes should result in an expected influx of freshmen intending to major
6:107:7722:24:24:72:197:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in the former categories.
6:108:7747:24:24:89:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Section 2 provides background information on the major choice literature and develops
6:109:7832:24:24:72:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:a theoretical framework for understanding how students should alter their major decisions
6:110:7921:24:24:72:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:after they observe economic downturns. Section 3 thoroughly describes the unique CIRP
6:111:8006:24:24:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:“Freshman Survey” data used to explore the relationship between freshmen intended major
6:112:8093:24:23:72:540:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and recessions. This section also describes the one key way this study differs from previous
6:113:8185:23:24:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:work by including national business cycle indicators as freshman major predictors. Section
6:114:8275:24:24:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:4 explains the multinomial logit empirical model used for the identification of a recession’s
6:115:8368:24:24:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:impact on freshman major choice. Section 5 reports the results using the previously outlined
6:116:8460:24:24:72:540:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:data and empirical model. In general, students are more likely to choose majors with better
6:117:8551:24:24:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:relative wages and employment opportunities after a they observe a recession. This is the
6:118:8640:24:24:72:540:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:first paper that can unambiguously confirm that to be true. Section 5 also explores different
6:119:8733:24:24:72:540:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:subsamples of the population, discussing how the major switching effect differs for males vs.
6:120:8826:24:54:72:372:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:females and blacks vs. whites. Lastly, Section 6 concludes.
6:121:8885:54:36:72:442:223:296:g_d0_f13:296:g_d0_f13:C:2  Background and Theoretical Framework
6:122:8924:36:24:72:540:187:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Because college major choice is pivotal for determining future career paths and earnings
6:123:9012:24:24:72:540:163:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:over a lifetime, a large literature focuses on understanding how students choose particular
6:124:9103:24:24:72:540:139:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:disciplines (Arcidiacono, 2004; Arcidiacono et al., 2010; Montmarquette, 2002; Beffy et al.,
6:125:9195:24:23:72:540:115:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:2010; Berger, 1988; Porter and Umbach, 2006; Dickson, 2010; Wisall and Zafar, 2012; Eide
6:126:9283:23:39:72:540:92:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and Waehrer 1998). Despite the extensive body of research on college major choice, no one
6:127:9372:39:0:303:309:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:4
7:128:9373:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:has unambiguously determined if and how the presence of a recession affects a student’s major
7:129:9466:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:preference. Because the business cycle informs many higher education decisions, isolating a
7:130:9557:24:24:72:488:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:pure major-switching effect to attribute to business cycle fluctuations is complex.
7:131:9640:24:24:89:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Fortunately, focusing on freshmen intended majors instead of college graduates’ majors
7:132:9726:24:24:72:539:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:simplifies matters, making identification of major-switching effects in the face of economic
7:133:9818:24:24:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:downturns analytically straightforward. There are only two potential business cycle effects
7:134:9909:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:that can alter the proportion of students observed across majors and that are present in a
7:135:9999:24:46:72:520:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:college freshman’s decision set: enrollment effects and intended major-switching effects.
7:136:10088:46:32:72:240:494:206:g_d0_f13:206:g_d0_f13:C:2.1  Enrollment Effects
7:137:10111:32:24:72:540:462:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Enrollment effects are any changes to the likelihoods of students majoring in certain disci-
7:138:10203:24:24:72:540:438:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:plines after changes in the business cycle and are a direct result of new and different types of
7:139:10299:24:24:72:540:414:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students enrolling in college. Numerous papers scrutinize how changes in the business cycle
7:140:10390:24:23:72:539:390:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:affect postsecondary enrollment rates (Mattila, 1982; Goldin, 1999; Sakellaris and Spilim-
7:141:10480:23:24:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:bergo, 2000; Card and Lemieuz, 1997), all finding that adverse business cycle conditions
7:142:10568:24:24:72:540:343:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:increase college enrollment rates. Students who are at the margin of enrolling in college and
7:143:10661:24:24:72:540:319:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:not enrolling in college are more likely to pursue postsecondary degrees if they observe the
7:144:10753:24:24:72:191:295:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:labor market declining.
7:145:10776:24:24:89:540:271:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Borrowing basic ideas from Manski and Wise (1983) and Lee (2010), the following model
7:146:10861:24:24:72:526:247:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:outlines a student’s choice between either entering the labor force or enrolling in college:
