13:287:21072:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:individual student characteristics as well as major-specific characteristics to model major
13:288:21163:24:24:72:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:choice. Lee’s findings are ambiguous and statistically insignificant for the majority of the
13:289:21255:24:24:72:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:cases he studies. This outcome could result because Lee is not working with a balanced
13:290:21341:24:24:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:panel; 80 percent of the students sampled made their major decisions in 1983 and are not
13:291:21429:24:23:72:275:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:observed after 1984, the threshold year.
13:292:21469:23:24:89:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The Integrated Postsecondary Education Data System (IPEDS) collects institutional-
13:293:21551:24:24:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:level data on the number of students graduating with degrees in different disciplines. These
13:294:21643:24:24:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:data are problematic because the intended majors of students beginning college are not
13:295:21729:24:24:72:540:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:observed, and it is hard to know whether changes in institutional proportions are a result of
13:296:21822:24:24:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:enrollment, major-switching, or a function of the time it takes students to graduate (Bradley,
13:297:21916:24:24:72:103:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:2012).
13:298:21922:24:24:89:540:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:An alternate data source that collects student major information over an extended
13:299:22003:24:24:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:time period is the Cooperative Institutional Research Program’s (CIRP’s) Freshman sur-
13:300:22089:24:24:72:540:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:vey housed in the Higher Education Research Institute (HERI) at the University of Cal-
13:301:22175:24:24:72:540:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:ifornia, Los Angeles (UCLA). These data have never before been used to investigate the
13:302:22261:24:23:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:relationship of student major and the business cycle, and this is the first paper to do so.
13:303:22352:23:24:72:540:182:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:These data have the advantage of observing freshmen intended majors before they enroll
13:304:22438:24:24:72:540:158:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in classes, so the identification of the major switching effect is not muddled by students’
13:305:22529:24:24:72:540:134:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:time-to-degree decisions (Bradley, 2012). In addition, the student-level nature of the data
13:306:22620:24:57:72:540:110:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:enables one to control for enrollment effects, addressing another identification problem of
13:307:22711:57:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:11
14:308:22713:0:47:72:261:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:previous approaches (Bradley, 2012).
14:309:22749:47:31:72:408:661:206:g_d0_f13:206:g_d0_f13:C:3.1  Higher Education Research Institute Data
14:310:22794:31:24:72:540:630:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Every year CIRP offers a survey of college freshmen that institutions can administer to their
14:311:22887:24:24:72:540:606:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students. Schools who opt into the survey must pay HERI a fee for the survey materials
14:312:22973:24:24:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and the data analysis provided after survey completion. HERI requires the survey to be
14:313:23059:24:24:72:540:558:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:administered to first-time, full-time freshmen before they begin fall semester classes.  As
14:314:23150:24:24:72:540:534:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:recommended by HERI, the large majority of institutions conduct the survey during their
14:315:23237:24:24:72:540:510:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:freshmen orientations in a proctored setting, ensuring the highest response rates and the
14:316:23326:24:24:72:214:486:143:g_d0_f8:64:g_d0_f20:B:most accurate information.5
14:317:23353:24:24:89:540:462:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Consequently, the majors observed in these data are intended majors of college freshmen
14:318:23440:24:24:72:540:438:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and not the majors with which students graduate, as in other data sources. This charac-
14:319:23527:24:24:72:540:414:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:teristic has both favorable and unfavorable implications for the research question at hand.
14:320:23618:24:23:72:540:390:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:First, because only intended majors are observable, students’ major preferences have not
14:321:23706:23:24:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:been altered by what they learn about the consumption values of majors in college. This
14:322:23793:24:24:72:540:343:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:type of information is irrelevant for this analysis, and if it can be eliminated, identification
14:323:23889:24:24:72:540:319:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:of major switching effect is more straightforward. However, because the majors with which
14:324:23978:24:24:72:539:295:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students graduate is not observable, it is more difficult to make conclusions about how the
14:325:24069:24:24:72:411:271:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:business cycles affect the general composition of the labor market.
14:326:24136:24:24:89:540:247:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:This particular study uses data from 191 institutions that participated in “The Freshman
14:327:24224:24:24:72:539:223:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Survey” thirty out of the thirty eight years from 1971-2008,6and where the state of the
14:328:24311:24:24:72:540:199:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:institution in observable. To protect the identity of the institutions, HERI requires that five
14:329:24406:24:18:72:540:175:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:or more institutions from the same state to be present in the sample before they reveal the
14:330:24497:18:15:85:539:157:49:g_d0_f9:99:g_d0_f10:F:5The “Freshman Survey” data obtained for research purposes are restricted access data and only granted
14:331:24599:15:12:72:540:142:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:to researchers after a thorough proposal process to ensure the identities of the institutions and the students
14:332:24709:12:8:72:132:130:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:are protected.
14:333:24723:8:0:85:291:122:49:g_d0_f9:99:g_d0_f10:F:6Data outside this date range were unavailable.
15:334:24772:0:41:72:238:708:143:g_d0_f8:64:g_d0_f20:B:state identity of the institution.7
15:335:24807:41:32:72:415:667:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f13:C:3.1.1  HERI Institutions Compared to a National Sample
15:336:24861:32:24:72:540:635:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Table 1 reports the composition of schools in the HERI sample used for analysis versus the
15:337:24951:24:24:72:539:611:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:national universe of four-year universities.8Private institutions account for 82.6 percent of
15:338:25044:24:23:72:540:587:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:all of the institutions in the HERI sample versus about 75.6 percent of all national insti-
15:339:25135:23:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:tutions. Because the cost of attending private universities is generally higher than the cost
15:340:25228:24:24:72:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:of attending public universities, the average student in the HERI sample might be more
15:341:25314:24:24:72:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:financially secure than the average college freshman. Strong evidence of this fact is reported
15:342:25408:24:24:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in Table 2 when student level characteristics are compared to a nationally representative
15:343:25497:24:24:72:211:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:sample of college freshmen.
15:344:25524:24:24:89:540:444:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:More importantly, the observed institutions in this study are more heavily weighted
15:345:25607:24:24:72:540:420:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:towards religious and liberal arts institutions than the nationally representative sample of
15:346:25699:24:24:72:540:396:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:institutions. The discrepancy in the proportion of liberal arts colleges has important implica-
15:347:25794:24:24:72:540:372:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:tions for this analysis because of the different experience average students have at liberal arts
15:348:25891:24:24:72:540:348:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:institutions versus at other types of private and public institutions. The Annapolis Group,
15:349:25982:24:23:72:540:324:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:an alliance of the majority of liberal arts colleges in the country, commissioned a study that
15:350:26076:23:24:72:540:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:found its graduates reported extreme differences in their college experience and the value
15:351:26166:24:24:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:of their college degrees compared to students at other types of private and flagship public
15:352:26257:24:24:72:540:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:institutions. For example, 87 percent of students at liberal arts colleges graduated in four
15:353:26349:24:24:72:540:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:years versus 76 percent at other private institutions and 51 percent of students at national
15:354:26441:24:24:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:flagship public institutions. Because students at liberal arts institutions graduate faster, on
15:355:26536:24:24:72:540:181:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:average, than students at other types of universities, liberal arts students are more likely to
15:356:26631:24:18:72:540:157:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:complete their degrees. Also, the intended majors with which they start will more closely
15:357:26720:18:15:85:539:139:49:g_d0_f9:99:g_d0_f10:F:7The states observed for the 191 institutions include CA, CT, GA, IL, IN, IA, MD, MA, MI, MN, MO,
15:358:26817:15:9:72:231:124:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:NY, NC, OH, PA, TX, VA, and WI.
15:359:26848:9:15:85:539:115:49:g_d0_f9:99:g_d0_f10:F:8Data for the national universe of schools come from IPEDS and theDigest of Education Statisticsfrom
15:360:26948:15:0:72:119:100:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:the NCES.
16:361:26959:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:mirror the majors with which they will graduate because they have less time to absorb the
16:362:27048:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:switching costs of changing majors (Brunello and Winter-Ember, 2003; Messer and Wolter,
16:363:27135:24:24:72:103:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:2007).
16:364:27141:24:24:89:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Furthermore, 79 percent of students who attended the liberal arts colleges in the survey
16:365:27229:24:24:72:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:reported the quality and breadth of academic preparation equipped them well for being
16:366:27314:24:24:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:accepted to graduate school or finding their first job. Only 73 percent of students at other
16:367:27406:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:private universities and 64 percent of students at national flagship public schools reported
16:368:27498:24:24:72:354:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the same level of preparation, respectively (Day, 2011).
16:369:27554:24:24:89:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Finally, the percentage of institutions classified as a Historically Black College or Uni-
16:370:27644:24:24:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:versity (HBCU) in the HERI sample is comparable to the national average, with 3.7 percent
16:371:27733:24:23:72:540:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in the HERI sample versus 3.9 percent, nationally. However, as reported in Table 2, there
16:372:27822:23:24:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:is a disparity in percentage of students in the sample identifying as black compared to the
16:373:27913:24:41:72:353:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:nationally representative proportion of black freshmen.
16:374:27968:41:32:72:398:380:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f13:C:3.1.2  HERI Students Compared to a National Sample
16:375:28018:32:24:72:540:348:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:One beneficial characteristic of the HERI data is the observable level of detail for student
16:376:28110:24:23:72:540:324:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:demographic characteristics. These characteristics are important major determinants and
16:377:28197:23:24:72:540:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:ones that should be measured to control for changes in enrollment when trying to identify
16:378:28286:24:24:72:539:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:major-switching effects. Montmarquett et al. (2002) find that women are less influenced
16:379:28373:24:24:72:540:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:than men by expected earnings when making their college major choice.  This finding is
16:380:28459:24:24:72:540:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:reasonable given that men are traditionally the main breadwinners of a household, so they are
16:381:28552:24:24:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:more sensitive to future earnings possibilities than women (Hamermesh and Donald, 2008).
16:382:28640:24:24:72:540:181:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Therefore, men are more likely than women to major in disciplines like Business, Engineering,
16:383:28733:24:24:72:540:157:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and Technology.  Wiswall and Zafar (2012) report strong taste parameter estimates for
16:384:28818:24:24:72:540:133:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:men in the Business and Economics disciplines and for women in the Arts and Humanities
16:385:28904:24:56:72:540:109:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:disciplines. Porter and Umbach (2006) cite several studies that confirm women are less likely
16:386:28997:56:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:14
17:387:28999:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:to major in the Sciences and Engineering than men and are more likely to major in fields
17:388:29087:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:like Education, Nursing, and the Humanities. Gender-role reinforcement and minority status
17:389:29177:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:within a discipline might be to blame for these observed gender differences (Lackland, 2001;
17:390:29269:24:24:72:146:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Kanter, 1993).
17:391:29283:24:24:89:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The same theories apply to why racial differences might affect major choice. Minority
17:392:29368:24:24:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students are less likely to choose a major where they are one of the few present in that major
17:393:29462:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:(Kanter, 1993). For this reason, there might be sorting on race by major as well. Dickson
17:394:29551:24:24:72:539:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:(2010),9who specifically studies race and gender differences in college major choice, finds a
17:395:29644:24:24:72:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:16 percentage point gap between white women compared to white men when examining the
17:396:29728:24:24:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:likelihoods of choosing Engineering and Technology majors. Additionally, white males are
17:397:29816:24:23:72:540:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:more likely to major in Business than white and Hispanic women and Asian and Hispanic
17:398:29901:23:24:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:males.  Furthermore, Dickson (2010) finds that women are more likely to major in the
17:399:29985:24:24:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Humanities than are men. Asians are less likely to major in the Humanities than whites
17:400:30071:24:24:72:539:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and Hispanics (Dickson, 2010). She cannot say anything about race and gender differences
17:401:30159:24:24:72:498:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in the Social Sciences because she uses that major category as her reference major.
17:402:30242:24:24:89:540:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Income and age are also important determinants in the major choice literature (Porter
17:403:30327:24:24:72:540:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and Umbach, 2006; Montmarquette et al. 2002; Berger, 1988). Students who have a higher
17:404:30413:24:24:72:540:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:relative family incomes may place less weight on the investment value of a major when
17:405:30498:24:24:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:choosing a major because they might have more family income to support them later in life.
17:406:30588:24:24:72:540:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:The opposite might be true for older more non-traditional students who may place more
17:407:30673:24:24:72:540:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:weight than the average student on the investment value of a major. Presumably, students
17:408:30761:24:23:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:who go back to school after taking time offmight care less about the consumption value of
17:409:30850:23:24:72:540:182:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:a college degree and might be more concerned with how their degree will impact their labor
17:410:30940:24:24:72:183:158:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:market opportunities.
17:411:30961:24:18:89:540:134:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:HERI provides a publicly available sample of students and sample weights that approx-
17:412:31046:18:16:85:540:116:49:g_d0_f9:99:g_d0_f10:F:9One difficulty in interpreting Dickson’s results is that she does not report race and gender likelihood
17:413:31150:16:0:72:400:100:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:coefficients separately but instead the interaction terms of race and gender.
18:414:31229:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:imate national trends for college freshmen through the year 1999.  To see if any strong
18:415:31316:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:student-level selection occurs in the data used for this paper, Table 2 compares the re-
18:416:31404:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:stricted access data provided by HERI for this study to the national trends for the years
18:417:31493:24:24:72:133:636:143:g_d0_f8:64:g_d0_f20:B:1980-1999.10
18:418:31505:24:24:89:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:In the freshmen survey data, income is reported as a categorical variable. Following the
18:419:31593:24:24:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:technique used in Hout (2004), income becomes a numeric variable by taking the midpoint
18:420:31680:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:of each category and converting it to 2008 dollars to adjust for inflation.  Age is also a
18:421:31770:24:24:72:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:categorical variable, but each category maps to a one year change in age, so this is not
18:422:31858:24:24:72:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:converted to actual age. The age category “3” maps to reporting an age of 18. Therefore,
18:423:31946:24:24:72:478:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the higher the age is above 3, the more non-traditional is the freshman sample.
18:424:32025:24:23:89:539:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:After conducting a difference in means test for the observable demographic variables, the
18:425:32114:23:24:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:differences between the two samples are confirmed as statistically significant, although they
18:426:32207:24:24:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:are not large. One option to address this selection problem is to weight the data to more
18:427:32296:24:24:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:closely resemble the national trends.  Unfortunately, all of the student and institutional-
18:428:32387:24:24:72:540:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:level variables required to apply the reported national norm weights cannot be observed.
18:429:32475:24:24:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Therefore, I must recognize how these samples differ to generalize my results to the national
18:430:32568:24:24:72:113:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:context.
18:431:32576:24:24:89:540:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Papers like Wiswall and Zafar (2011) are also unable to weight their sample to more
18:432:32659:24:24:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:closely resemble the population. They address this problem by recognizing the differences in
18:433:32751:24:24:72:540:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the two samples and discussing how those differences might affect the results when students
18:434:32842:24:24:72:540:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:are selecting a major. In the present context, because the sample has a greater percentage of
18:435:32935:24:17:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:private and liberal arts institutions, the students are richer, whiter, of more traditional age,
18:436:33031:17:16:81:539:188:49:g_d0_f9:99:g_d0_f10:F:10Although intended major and the other important demographic characteristics are observable for the
18:437:33131:16:12:72:540:172:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:years 1971-2008, I only use data for 1980-2008 in the final model. The identification strategy used in this
18:438:33238:12:12:72:540:160:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:paper is not feasible with long periods of economic turmoil and little recovery. As discussed in the next
18:439:33343:12:12:72:540:148:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:section, identification of the major switching effect relies on periods of negative economic shocks followed by
18:440:33454:12:12:72:540:136:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:observable periods of recovery, like the period of stagflation in the 1970s. Because the 1970s is viewed as a
18:441:33563:12:12:72:540:124:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:entire decade of economic turmoil, including these years in the model muddles the identification of major
18:442:33668:12:59:72:145:112:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:switching effects.
18:443:33686:59:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:16
19:444:33688:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and more likely female than a more nationally-representative sample of students. Although
19:445:33777:24:24:72:539:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the students in this sample do differ slightly from the representative sample, the direction
19:446:33869:24:24:72:539:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:of the differences turns out to be quite fortunate. A more representative sample of students
19:447:33961:24:24:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:would be more likely to change their majors after recessions than students in this sample
19:448:34050:24:24:72:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:because, as outlined previously in this section, male, minority, poorer and older students
19:449:34140:24:24:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:care more about the investment value of a major than do their counterparts. Therefore,
19:450:34226:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the effects in this study can be viewed as conservative estimates of major switching after
19:451:34316:24:24:72:385:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:recessions compared to a national sample of college students.
19:452:34377:24:24:89:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:While the CIRP “Freshman Survey” data provide a broad range of student demographic
19:453:34459:24:24:72:539:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:information, one disadvantage is that response rates differ for all variables collected. Only
19:454:34552:24:23:72:540:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:variables for which there are high response rates over the entire sample period can be included
19:455:34647:23:24:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in the model because of fears of sample selection based on survey nonresponse. Table 3 lists
19:456:34739:24:24:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:response rates for those in my model: gender, race, income, and age.  All the variables
19:457:34826:24:24:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:listed have student response rates of over 89 percent of the sample. These response rates
19:458:34915:24:24:72:540:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:are comparable for the nationally representative sample provided by HERI. Therefore, there
19:459:35005:24:24:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:is no reason to believe that response rates for students in my sample would differ from the
19:460:35096:24:41:72:330:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:response rates from students in a national sample.
19:461:35146:41:31:72:331:284:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f13:C:3.1.3  HERI data and Major Heterogeneity
19:462:35186:31:24:72:540:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:This analysis considers thirteen major categories. Table 4 details high-wage majors versus
19:463:35276:24:24:72:555:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:low-wage majors and high-employment-opportunity majors versus low-employment-opportunity
19:464:35364:24:24:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:majors, as outlined in Section 2.2 of the paper. The Education major is unique because it
19:465:35453:24:24:72:540:181:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:is considered a low-wage major and a high-employment-opportunity major, so it is unclear
19:466:35541:24:24:72:540:157:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:how students will respond to this major when they observe business cycle shocks. Figure 1
19:467:35630:24:24:72:540:133:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:displays the proportions of students intending to major in each discipline averaged over all
19:468:35722:24:56:72:174:109:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:years in the sample.
19:469:35742:56:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:17
20:470:35744:0:24:89:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:As mentioned in Section 3.1.2, a student’s demographic characteristics are critical for
20:471:35831:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:determining which major a student chooses. Table 5 summarizes important demographic
20:472:35914:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:characteristics by major; this table provides cursory evidence that students indeed sort into
20:473:36007:24:24:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:majors across income, age, gender and race. In general, richer students sort into majors
20:474:36095:24:24:72:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:with lower wages and lower job market opportunities like English, History, Humanities, and
20:475:36185:24:24:72:159:588:143:g_d0_f8:64:g_d0_f20:B:Social Sciences.11
20:476:36203:24:24:89:539:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The summary statistics by major for age, gender, and race also reveal expected trends.
20:477:36289:24:24:72:541:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Older (more non-traditional) freshmen major in high-wage and high-employment-opportunity
20:478:36377:24:24:72:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:majors that are less likely to require graduate study such as Technology, Engineering, Busi-
20:479:36469:24:24:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:ness, and Education.  Presumably, an older student is less likely to return to college to
20:480:36558:24:23:72:540:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:major in something that has a lower investment value after graduation. Furthermore, there
20:481:36647:23:24:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:is a larger share of male students majoring in Engineering, Technology, Physical Sciences,
20:482:36737:24:24:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Business, Math, and History, respectively, than their share of the total freshmen population.
20:483:36830:24:24:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:This conforms to what Mountmarquette et al.  (2002) proposes: males care more about
20:484:36913:24:24:72:303:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:investment values of majors than do females.
20:485:36957:24:24:89:540:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Asian students constitute more than their representative share in the Biology, Health,
20:486:37043:24:24:72:540:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Engineering, Technology, Physical Sciences, and Math majors. Black freshmen report in-
20:487:37129:24:24:72:540:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:tended majors at higher rates in Technology, Health, Social Sciences, Biology, and Business
20:488:37220:24:24:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:fields. Finally, white students represent more than their total share of the population in
20:489:37310:24:24:72:524:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Education, English, Humanities, Mathematics, Physical Sciences, History, and Business.
20:490:37396:24:24:89:540:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Table 6, which ranks majors by average student high school GPA, summarizes how certain
20:491:37482:24:23:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students sort into majors based on ability levels. This information conforms to what previous
20:492:37575:23:24:72:539:182:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:studies report about how a student’s ability affects her major choice. HERI reports GPA on
20:493:37665:24:24:72:540:158:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:a 1-8 scale with 1 being a D, 8 being an A, and 5 being a B. The mean for all student is
20:494:37753:24:18:72:540:134:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:around a 6.1, or a B+ according to their scale. Those who perform better on average in high
20:495:37844:18:16:81:539:116:49:g_d0_f9:99:g_d0_f10:F:11The Business major is the exception and the only high-family-income major in the top 5 that is not
20:496:37944:16:0:72:332:100:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:considered a low-wage, low-employment-opportunity major.
21:497:38002:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:school choose more technical majors like Math, Physical Sciences, Biology, and Engineering.
21:498:38093:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:The variables Academic, Art, Math, Write, and Confidence are student self reported ability
21:499:38183:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:scores in these areas on a scale of 1-6. It is clear that students sort into majors for which
21:500:38276:24:24:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:they believe they have the highest abilities. Response rates are not high enough for many
21:501:38365:24:24:72:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:of these variables over a long enough time period for them to be included in the empirical
21:502:38455:24:24:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:model, but this table provides interesting information on which types of students choose
21:503:38543:24:46:72:149:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:certain majors.
21:504:38558:46:32:72:253:518:206:g_d0_f13:206:g_d0_f13:C:3.2  Business Cycle Data
21:505:38582:32:24:72:540:486:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:To correctly identify the effects of observed recessions on students’ major decisions, the
21:506:38672:24:24:72:540:462:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:business cycle variables must capture the information shock of an economic downturn. The
21:507:38760:24:24:72:540:438:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:few previous papers that have asked a similar question have used a variety of data to model
21:508:38851:24:24:72:540:414:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the business cycle which signal both changes in expected future earnings and labor market
21:509:38940:24:23:72:540:390:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:opportunities (Lee, 2010; Bradley, 2012). Lee (2010) uses the most comprehensive set of
21:510:39027:23:24:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:business cycle variables. Employing indicators for wages and unemployment at the national
21:511:39116:24:24:72:540:343:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and state levels, and obtains ambiguous results. Because there are so many business cycle
21:512:39205:24:24:72:539:319:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:variables in Lee’s model, it is analytically intractable for him to try to parse out the effects of
21:513:39304:24:24:72:540:295:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the information shock of the recession on student major choice. The timing of fluctuations in
21:514:39397:24:24:72:540:271:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:wages and unemployment is syncopated during a recession, with increases in unemployment
21:515:39484:24:24:72:540:247:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:usually lagging behind decreases in wages. It is perilous to speculate to which movements in
21:516:39576:24:24:72:540:223:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:these variables students are more likely to respond because previous studies show that both
21:517:39667:24:24:72:369:199:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:factors play important roles in a student’s major decision.
21:518:39726:24:24:89:539:175:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:In addition, student responses to certain economic indicators are not expected to be to
21:519:39813:24:24:72:540:151:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:be symmetric. For example, how students’ major choices respond to a 3 percent increase
21:520:39899:24:23:72:540:127:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in unemployment when unemployment is initially 4 percent might be different than how
21:521:39983:23:51:72:540:104:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students change their major decisions when initial unemployment is 8 percent. Fortunately,
21:522:40073:51:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:19
22:523:40075:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the recession troughs reported by the National Bureau of Economic Research’s (NBER’s)
22:524:40160:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Business Cycle Dating Committee are business cycle indicators that capture both changes
22:525:40247:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:to wages and unemployment and allow for student response asymmetry.  The recession
22:526:40329:24:24:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:troughs are the periods where national recessions are thought to bottom out before they
22:527:40416:24:24:72:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:begin periods of recovery. The NBER has no fixed definition of what determines trough dates
22:528:40507:24:24:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and uses various measures of broad economic activity in its analysis: real GDP, economy-
22:529:40595:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:wide employment, and real income. The committee may also use sector specific information
22:530:40683:24:24:72:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in its evaluation. The trough years observed for the sample period used in this model are
22:531:40772:24:24:72:221:516:143:g_d0_f8:64:g_d0_f20:B:1980, 1982, 1991, and 2001.12
22:532:40801:24:24:89:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Figures 2-4 show how major proportions are changing over time with trough years indi-
22:533:40886:24:23:72:540:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:cated in the graph. After trough years, defined kinks appear in the reported major proportion
22:534:40979:23:24:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:lines, which simply provides suggestive evidence that students are in some way responding
22:535:41068:24:24:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:to this new information. Employing a full econometric model that controls for other factors
22:536:41159:24:24:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:that influence college major choice is the next step in determining how students respond to
22:537:41250:24:54:72:251:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:adverse business cycle information.
22:538:41285:54:36:72:243:319:296:g_d0_f13:296:g_d0_f13:C:4  Empirical Model
22:539:41303:36:24:72:540:283:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:This analysis uses a multinomial logit technique similar to that used in Dickson (2010)
22:540:41390:24:24:72:540:259:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and Porter and Umbach (2006). Taking individual student level variables from the CIRP
22:541:41475:24:24:72:540:235:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:“Freshman Survey” along with the recession trough data from the NBER, I estimate the
22:542:41559:24:45:72:391:211:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:following empirical model for freshman intended major choice:
22:543:41620:45:0:240:315:166:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f8:A:Pr(Mi=j)=
22:544:41629:0:0:332:342:174:143:g_d0_f17:64:g_d0_f22:C:eβ
22:545:41631:0:8:343:345:185:36:g_d0_f25:36:g_d0_f25:F:′
22:546:41632:8:12:342:354:177:36:g_d0_f26:36:g_d0_f26:F:jxi
22:547:41635:12:13:316:336:165:143:g_d0_f19:64:g_d0_f18:C:∑K
22:548:41637:13:0:329:352:152:64:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f17:C:k=0e
22:549:41641:0:23:352:370:160:64:g_d0_f22:36:g_d0_f26:F:β′kxi
22:550:41646:23:16:81:539:137:49:g_d0_f9:99:g_d0_f10:F:12I considered using state-level business cycle indicators in addition to national recession troughs, but
22:551:41751:16:68:72:499:121:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:similar to the results seen in Lee (2010), no coherent story develops for these state-level variables.
22:552:41853:68:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:20
23:553:41855:0:24:72:86:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:for
23:554:41858:24:35:254:356:684:143:g_d0_f17:143:g_d0_f17:C:j=0,1,2,3,4, ..., K
23:555:41877:35:24:71:540:649:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:where K is the number of broad intended major categories in the data.Mis the intended
23:556:41962:24:24:71:539:625:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:major choice of the student, which is a function of the demographic and time series variables
23:557:42055:24:24:71:539:601:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:included in vectorX.Xalso includes year and state dummy variables, and university trend
23:558:42142:24:24:71:127:577:143:g_d0_f8:64:g_d0_f20:B:variables.13
23:559:42154:24:24:89:540:553:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:By controlling for demographic characteristics, this empirical strategy compares similar
23:560:42242:24:23:71:539:529:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students across time to assess whether or not the presence of a recession has any real effect on
23:561:42338:23:24:71:539:506:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the majors students choose. If different types of students are enrolling in college after they
23:562:42432:24:24:71:539:482:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:observe recessions, controlling for observable demographic characteristics partially alleviates
23:563:42527:24:24:71:539:458:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:this issue to allow for more precise identification of the major-switching effect. If, however,
23:564:42622:24:24:71:539:434:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:certain unobservable student characteristics are potentially correlated with major choice
23:565:42711:24:24:71:539:410:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:after recessions, then I must use techniques to hypothesize the direction of these effects to
23:566:42804:24:24:71:323:386:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:appropriately bound any major-switching effects.
23:567:42852:24:24:89:540:362:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:In addition, the school a student attends undoubtedly influences major choice. For exam-
23:568:42940:24:24:71:539:338:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:ple, a student attending the Georgia Institute of Technology is much more likely to choose an
23:569:43033:24:24:71:539:314:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Engineering major than a student attending the University of Georgia. The large number of
23:570:43122:24:24:71:539:290:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:major categories and the computationally intensive multinomial logit routine does not make
23:571:43212:24:23:71:539:266:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:it analytically tractable to add 191 institutional dummy variables, so I determine the average
23:572:43306:23:24:71:539:243:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:number of students over time at each institution majoring in the different major categories
23:573:43397:24:16:71:539:219:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and include those control variables in the model. This is the first best alternative that also
23:574:43491:16:15:81:539:203:49:g_d0_f9:99:g_d0_f10:F:13One important identifying assumption for the multinomial logit model is independence of irrelevant
23:575:43591:15:12:72:540:188:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:alternatives (IIA). This assumption claims that the odds of preferring one major over another do not depend
23:576:43698:12:12:72:540:176:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:on the presence or absence of other irrelevant majors. Previous papers that use multinomial or conditional
23:577:43804:12:12:72:540:164:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:logit to model major choice fail to test for this IIA assumption (Porter and Umbach, 2006; Dickson, 2010;
23:578:43909:12:12:72:540:152:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:and Lee, 2010). However, Lee (2010) mentions that even in the presence of an endogenous choice set (or
23:579:44011:12:12:72:540:140:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:a violation of IIA) his model would return consistent parameter estimates. I test the validity of the IIA
23:580:44116:12:12:72:540:128:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:assumption using the Hausman-McFadden test. The test suggest that some of the majors fail to meet the
23:581:44217:12:12:72:540:116:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:IIA condition. I can collapse on more similar majors in future iterations of this paper using nested logit,
23:582:44324:12:51:72:527:104:99:g_d0_f10:99:g_d0_f10:F:which relaxes the IIA assumption. For now, the relative risk ratios are reported using multinomial logit.
23:583:44429:51:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:21
24:584:44431:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:captures any proclivity a student may have for a particular major given the institution he
24:585:44521:24:24:72:148:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:or she attends.
24:586:44536:24:24:89:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:My model differs from previous models asking this question by including national business
24:587:44625:24:24:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:cycle troughs. Contemporaneous and lagged dummy variables for recession troughs, allow
24:588:44711:24:24:72:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:me to estimate the change in the relative risk ratios (rrr’s) of different freshmen major
24:589:44800:24:24:71:539:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:intentions relative to a reference major. Ifrrr >1, then the average student is many times
24:590:44890:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:more likely to choose that major during a trough year compared to the reference major,
24:591:44976:24:24:72:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and if therrr <1, then a student is less likely to choose that major during a trough year
24:592:45065:24:24:72:242:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:compared to the reference major.
24:593:45097:24:24:89:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The results are reported asrrr’s between the remaining majors and the reference major,
24:594:45183:24:23:72:540:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:English. The English intended major possesses a steady share of the student totals over time.
24:595:45276:23:24:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:As shown in Figure 4, the share of English majors was 2.0 percent in 1980 and 2.7 percent
24:596:45365:24:24:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in 2008. The proportion never deviates by more than 0.6 percentage points away from its
24:597:45452:24:24:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:mean of 2.6. English does not appear to fall victim to the cyclical choice pattern that seems
24:598:45545:24:24:72:540:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:to plague other majors. Therefore, students are less likely to switch into or out of that major
24:599:45640:24:24:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:when business cycle fluctuations occur, making the English major a good reference point.
24:600:45728:24:24:72:540:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Also, according to Table 5, English majors are the richest students compared to their peers
24:601:45819:24:24:72:540:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in other majors; they might care less about the investment value of majors because they
24:602:45906:24:24:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:potentially have more financial support from their families. Additionally, because English is
24:603:45999:24:24:72:540:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:seen as a typically low-wage and low-employment opportunity major, theory suggests that
24:604:46086:24:24:72:540:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:this would not be a major the marginal student would want to choose after observing a
24:605:46171:24:23:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:recession. Imagine instead a major like Business as the reference major. It would prove
24:606:46258:23:24:72:540:182:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:challenging to hypothesize the direction of the relative risk of Engineering majors relative to
24:607:46353:24:24:72:119:158:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Business.
24:608:46362:24:24:89:540:134:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The contemporaneous trough indicator is the variable of interest in the model.  The
24:609:46445:24:57:72:540:110:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:direction of the relative risk ratio for this variable will most closely capture the major-
24:610:46536:57:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:22
25:611:46538:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:switching effect. The contemporaneous business cycle variable is less likely to contain any
25:612:46629:24:24:72:539:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:enrollment effect because it is difficult for students to observe a recession and decide to enroll
25:613:46727:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in a four-year university in the same year. Strong enrollment effect should materialize in the
25:614:46821:24:24:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:lags of trough variables because it takes time to apply to and be accepted into a four-year
25:615:46912:24:24:72:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:university; Typically, students decide whether they are going to college by the year prior to
25:616:47005:24:24:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:enrollment. Four lags of the trough variables are included in the model to also control for
25:617:47096:24:54:72:182:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:any enrollment effect.
25:618:47118:54:36:72:163:510:296:g_d0_f13:296:g_d0_f13:C:5  Results
25:619:47128:36:24:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:A logit model for student decisions to declare an intended major reveals that freshmen are
25:620:47218:24:24:72:540:450:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:more likely to report an intended major in a trough year than in a non-trough year. The log
25:621:47309:24:24:72:540:426:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:odds of not declaring an intended major versus declaring an intended major falls by .48 in
25:622:47399:24:24:72:540:402:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:a trough year. Therefore, I estimate the main empirical model conditional on declaring an
25:623:47488:24:23:72:540:378:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:intended major, using the freshmen whose relevant demographic information (gender, race,
25:624:47576:23:24:72:364:355:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:age, and income) is observable from the years 1980-2008.
25:625:47632:24:24:89:539:331:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The results conform to what theory and anecdotal evidence suggest: students alter their
25:626:47719:24:24:72:540:307:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:college major intentions when they observe shocks to the business cycle. This is the first
25:627:47809:24:24:72:540:283:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:paper that can unambiguously declare the direction in which students alter their major
25:628:47895:24:24:72:539:259:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:intentions during a recession. Table 7 reports a summary of the relative risk ratios (rrr’s)
25:629:47987:24:24:71:539:235:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:for the contemporaneous trough variable for each of the twelve major categories compared
25:630:48075:24:24:71:539:211:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:to the reference major English. The full multinomial logit output can be found in Appendix
25:631:48165:24:24:71:539:187:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Tables A1-A10. As previously stated, the focus remains on the contemporaneous business
25:632:48251:24:24:71:539:163:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:cycle term to identify the major-switching effects; it is this term that, theoretically, is least
25:633:48348:24:24:71:224:139:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:affected by enrollment effects.
25:634:48379:24:23:89:540:115:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The first column in Table 7 lists the rank and magnitude of the relative risk ratios
25:635:48463:23:39:71:539:92:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:of the contemporaneous trough variable for the majors over the full sample of freshmen
25:636:48549:39:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:23
26:637:48551:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:included in the model. The second column lists the majors’ rankings and magnitudes of
26:638:48636:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the contemporaneous trough for females, the third column for males, the fourth column
26:639:48721:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:for whites, and the fifth column for blacks.  Table 8 displays the tiers of majors whose
26:640:48809:24:24:72:539:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:magnitudes are not statistically different from one another.14If majors are in the same
26:641:48896:24:24:71:539:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:tier, one cannot decipher which of the majors the students would prefer, on average, after a
26:642:48988:24:24:71:539:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:recession. However, if two majors are in different tiers, then, on average, students prefer a
26:643:49081:24:24:71:342:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:major in the higher of the two tiers after a recession.
26:644:49136:24:24:89:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:A recession’s effect on the likelihood that students will choose Technology is the strongest
26:645:49228:24:24:71:539:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:for the full sample of students, as well as for each subgroup. Institutions should expect an
26:646:49320:24:24:71:539:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:increase in the demand for classes required for a Technology major after a recession. This
26:647:49410:24:23:71:539:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:is an interesting result because Technology classes are some of the most expensive classes
26:648:49500:23:24:71:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:to offer, given the resources required.  This should be a particular concern for university
26:649:49591:24:24:71:444:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:administrators, given their strained budgets during economic downturns.
26:650:49662:24:24:89:539:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Unsurprisingly, Business and Engineering majors fall into the second tier of increased
26:651:49748:24:24:71:539:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:major demand across the full sample and all subsamples. The Social Science major never rises
26:652:49840:24:24:71:539:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:above the penultimate tier for any of the subgroups, which is expected given that it is a low-
26:653:49934:24:24:71:539:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:wage, low-employment opportunity major. In general, the rankings of the majors conform
26:654:50020:24:24:71:539:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:to theoretical priors. Majors that typically pay higher wages and have more employment
26:655:50106:24:24:71:540:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:opportunities have largerrrr’s relative to English majors, and majors for which wages and
26:656:50195:24:24:71:539:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:employment opportunities are not as substantial have smaller magnitudes relative to the
26:657:50282:24:24:71:154:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:reference major.
26:658:50298:24:23:89:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The major rankings are fairly consistent across columns in Table 7 with varying mag-
26:659:50382:23:24:71:539:182:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:nitudes. The Education major ranks higher for females compared to males, as expected,
26:660:50467:24:24:71:539:158:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:and the Health major ranks higher for males compared to females. The magnitudes of the
26:661:50553:24:18:71:539:134:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:relative risk ratios is partially a function of the number of students choosing that major on
26:662:50646:18:0:81:518:116:49:g_d0_f9:99:g_d0_f10:F:14The majors in the same tiers for the same model have overlapping 95 percent confidence intervals.
27:663:50747:0:24:72:539:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:average in that category. Therefore, the very largerrrfor females and Technology majors
27:664:50834:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:is most likely a result of the small number female technology majors, on average. However,
27:665:50924:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:therrr’s for black students are higher in every category, which implies that black students
27:666:51015:24:24:72:539:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:care more about recessions than white students when making their college major decisions.
27:667:51104:24:24:89:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The Fine Arts and Biology majors stand out as the two exceptions to the hypothesis that
27:668:51191:24:24:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:high-wage, high-employment majors will be preferred after recessions. Previous psycholog-
27:669:51280:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:ical literature suggests that the result for Fine Arts majors is not as odd as it may seem.
27:670:51371:24:24:72:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Csikszentmihalyi and Getzels (1973) report that Fine Arts majors compared to students who
27:671:51460:24:24:72:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:major in other disciplines have low levels of “superego strength” which indicates that these
27:672:51552:24:24:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students do not conform to cultural or social standards. They also describe artists as “reso-
27:673:51645:24:23:72:540:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:lute and accustomed to making their own decisions.” Shelton and Harris (1979) confirm that
27:674:51735:23:24:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:those who major in the Arts possess an “assertive boldness.” Students who choose to major
27:675:51824:24:24:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in Art already know they are making a risky financial decision and are probably students
27:676:51912:24:24:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:that place a very low priority on the investment value of their college major. That weight is
27:677:52005:24:24:72:540:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:unlikely to change by enough after a recession to induce them to switch majors to another
27:678:52094:24:24:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:field. Therefore, any shocks to investment value, like a recession, would have no visible effect
27:679:52190:24:24:72:540:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:on their decision to be an Art major. It is probably not the case that more students are
27:680:52278:24:24:72:540:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:majoring in Fine Arts after a recession, but instead the exact same students who chose an
27:681:52367:24:24:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Art major before a recession are going to choose an Art major after a recession. If there are
27:682:52460:24:24:72:540:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:any changes at all in the number of students choosing to major in English after a recession,
27:683:52552:24:24:72:285:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:then therrr >1 for the Fine Arts major.
27:684:52591:24:23:89:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The unexpected results for Biology majors are more difficult to explain.  Combining
27:685:52674:23:24:72:540:182:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:evidence from Arcidiacono et al. (2010) and Stinebrickner and Stinebrickner (2011), students
27:686:52766:24:24:72:540:158:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:would prefer to major in less challenging disciplines,ceteris paribus. When students receive
27:687:52858:24:24:72:540:134:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:updated information, many times they choose to change out of the more technical majors like
27:688:52949:24:57:72:540:110:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Math and Science to majors like Humanities and Social Sciences. If students’ expectations
27:689:53038:57:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:25
28:690:53040:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:are altered so that the investment value to Biology majors after a recession changes its relative
28:691:53137:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:rank in the major spectrum, then students might switch out of Biology majors into fields
28:692:53225:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:that are less challenging. Stinebrickner and Stinebrickner (2011) also show that students are
28:693:53318:24:24:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:not very likely to switch into a Biology major after receiving updated information but, most
28:694:53410:24:24:72:281:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:of the time, will switch out of the major.
28:695:53452:24:24:89:539:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:There might be concern that some enrollment effects are present in the contemporaneous
28:696:53538:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:trough term.  Each demographic variable can be regressed on the remaining variables in
28:697:53624:24:24:72:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the model. By observing the magnitude and the significance level of the contemporaneous
28:698:53711:24:24:72:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:trough term and if there are priors about the direction of correlation between the observable
28:699:53804:24:24:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:demographic variables and any unobservable variables, then any remaining enrollment effects
28:700:53895:24:23:72:540:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:can be signed.  Table 10 reports the results for the OLS regressions of the demographic
28:701:53982:23:24:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:variables on the other variables in the empirical model. The contemporaneous trough for
28:702:54069:24:24:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:males and whites are positive and significant meaning that in trough years more males and
28:703:54158:24:24:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:whites enroll in school. The contemporanous trough variable is negative and significant for
28:704:54249:24:24:72:540:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:age and income. This is not surprising if older students choose not to enroll in school in
28:705:54339:24:24:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:trough years and that the average student is poorer in a trough year. Even though there
28:706:54426:24:24:72:539:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:appear to be enrollment effects across these variables, these should not affect the estimated
28:707:54519:24:24:72:539:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:major-switching effects because these variables are controlled for in the multinomial logit
28:708:54610:24:24:72:106:277:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:model.
28:709:54616:24:24:89:540:253:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Table 11 reports OLS regression results for some of the variables not included in the
28:710:54701:24:24:72:540:229:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:multinomial logit model because of their low response rates in the HERI survey. Students
28:711:54789:24:23:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:have lower high school GPAs, SAT Math scores, and SAT Verbal scores in business cycle
28:712:54874:23:24:72:540:182:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:trough years. Because these ability measures are not included in the model, these enroll-
28:713:54963:24:24:72:539:158:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:ment effects might bias the results of the major-switching effects.  However, since lower
28:714:55052:24:24:72:540:134:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:ability students usually choose low-wage and low-employment opportunity majors, the esti-
28:715:55141:24:57:72:540:110:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:mated major-switching effects should be interpreted as lower bounds if these student ability
28:716:55233:57:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:26
29:717:55235:0:24:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:enrollment effects are present One exception to this would be the Business major. Business
29:718:55325:24:24:72:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:is a high-wage, high-employment opportunity major and also a major that lower ability
29:719:55410:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students prefer.  The estimates of the major-switching effects for Business therefore may
29:720:55499:24:24:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:be overestimated and should be interpreted as a combined major-switching and enrollment
29:721:55586:24:24:72:102:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:effect.
29:722:55593:24:24:89:539:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The relativerrr’s for the first through fourth lags of the trough variable are reported in
29:723:55683:24:24:71:539:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:the Appendix Tables A1-A10. It is important to interpret these ratios as a combination of
29:724:55772:24:24:71:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:enrollment effects and major switching effects. When the direction of therrrrelationship
29:725:55860:24:24:72:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:changes for the lags of the trough variable compared to the contemporaneous term, then the
29:726:55950:24:24:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:enrollment effect and major switching effect are thought to be moving in different directions
29:727:56043:24:54:72:269:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:with the enrollment effect dominating.
29:728:56081:54:36:72:194:414:296:g_d0_f13:296:g_d0_f13:C:6  Conclusion
29:729:56094:36:23:72:540:378:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:This is the first paper to empirically show an unambiguous relationship between the business
29:730:56186:23:24:72:540:355:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:cycle and the majors that college students choose. First, this study finds that freshmen are
29:731:56278:24:24:72:540:331:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:less likely to have an undeclared intended major during a recession trough. Those who do
29:732:56366:24:24:72:540:307:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:report an intended major during a recession are generally more likely to choose majors that
29:733:56457:24:24:72:540:283:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:pay higher wages and have more job security like Technology, Business, Engineering, and
29:734:56544:24:24:72:540:259:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:Health majors. Finally, lower ability students are more likely to enroll in college during a
29:735:56636:24:24:72:540:235:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:recession. These students are more likely to choose low-wage, low-employment opportunity
29:736:56724:24:24:72:540:211:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:majors which might also bias the major-switching effects for high-wage, high-employment
29:737:56811:24:24:72:235:187:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:opportunity majors downwards.
29:738:56840:24:24:89:540:163:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:The results of this paper should be interpreted as conservative estimates of student major-
29:739:56931:24:24:72:540:139:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:switching responses after recessions, as this sample is more heavily weighted towards wealthy,
29:740:57025:24:23:72:540:115:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:white, female, and liberal arts students. A more nationally representative sample than the
29:741:57115:23:39:72:540:92:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:CIRP “Freshman Survey” might more closely capture an average student’s response to a
29:742:57199:39:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:27
30:743:57201:0:24:72:120:708:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:recession.
30:744:57211:24:24:89:540:684:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:This paper helps researchers to better understand how students make their major deci-
30:745:57296:24:24:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:sions. Because of data limitations, previous studies have been unable to identify whether
30:746:57385:24:24:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:students respond to business cycle signals when choosing college majors.  The data used
30:747:57472:24:24:72:540:612:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:here improve upon the student-level college major data and introduce a new variable that
30:748:57560:24:24:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:characterizes the business cycle. While recession troughs may seem like obvious business
30:749:57648:24:24:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:cycle indicators, previous papers focus on levels of wages and unemployment. Students may
30:750:57737:24:24:72:540:540:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:not initially have perfect information about wage and unemployment variables to factor into
30:751:57828:24:24:72:540:516:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:their major decisions. However, students should have a basic understanding of how the econ-
30:752:57919:24:24:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:omy is performing, and this is best captured by the recession trough data from the NBER.
30:753:58007:24:23:72:540:468:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:The information shock of a recession trough induces students to switch their intended majors
30:754:58099:23:24:72:384:445:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:in the direction that theory and anecdotal evidence suggests.
30:755:58160:24:24:89:540:421:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:Knowing the types of majors students are more likely to choose during recessions helps
30:756:58246:24:24:72:540:397:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:administrators plan for fluctuations across field of study. University administrators armed
30:757:58337:24:24:72:540:373:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:with the information of a recession’s major-switching effects can then allocate resources
30:758:58426:24:24:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:accordingly. Also, if economists and other researchers know how students switch their majors
30:759:58518:24:24:72:540:325:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:during recession years, then the forecasting of labor market shortages and surpluses in certain
30:760:58613:24:248:72:241:301:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:B:fields will become more accurate.
30:761:58646:248:0:300:312:53:143:g_d0_f8:143:g_d0_f8:A:28
